┼Ыr─лniv─Бsa-m┼лrti-prast─Бvaс╕е

With prose order in Sanskrit and English Translation

рд╢реНрд░реА рдЕрдкреНрдкрдпреНрдпрджреАрдХреНрд╖рд┐рддрд░рдЪрд┐рдд
рд╡рд░рджрд░рд╛рдЬрд╕реНрддрд╡рдГ

Preface

Varadar─Бjastavaс╕е is a beautiful hymn in Sanskrit to the deity Varadar─Бja of K─Бnc─лpuram, Tamil n─Бс╕Нu composed by the erudite scholar and poet Appayyad─лkс╣гita who lived in the late 16th and early 17th centuries. The poetтАЩs birth place was not far from K─Бnc─лpuram.

Appayyad─лkс╣гita who is famous for his work Kuvalay─Бnanda, a treatise on poetics (alaс╣Еk─Бra┼Ы─Бstram) was a staunch follower of monism (advaita) yet displayed a liberal attitude towards great persons and great works antagonistic to Monism. He wrote a commentary on the epic Y─Бdav─Бbhyudayam of Ved─Бntade┼Ыika , who was one of the foremost proponents of Qualified Monism (Vi┼Ыiс╣гс╣н─Бdvaita). Although Appayyad─лkс╣гita was a ┼Ъaivite (worshipper of ┼Ъiva) he has composed this hymn on Varadar─Бja, a deity representing Viс╣гс╣Зu thus demonstrating his catholicity. Actually in those days inter-marriages between worshippers of ┼Ъiva and worshippers of Viс╣гс╣Зu were not uncommon and it is said that Appayyad─лkс╣гitaтАЩs fatherтАЩs mother came from a ┼Ъrivaiс╣гс╣Зavite family.

In addition to writing classic treatises on poetics, Appayyad─лkс╣гita has written several profound works on Advaita, Vi┼Ыiс╣гс╣н─Бdvaita and Dvaita (dualism). He has also enriched devotional literature by composing several hymns on deities.

The author has provided his own commentary for this hymn, which helps in understanding the verses as intended by the author. Sri Appayyad─лkс╣гita himself appears to have considered this beautiful short hymn as one of his best literary works as several verses of this hymn are quoted by the poet in his Kuvalay─Бnada. It is not surprising that as a well-known authority on poetics he has woven in the verses of this hymn intricate patterns of alaс╣Еk─Бras. While the poet leads the reader through the city of K─Бnc─л to the temple-enclosures, the flight of steps to the temple and the LordтАЩs bewitching form slowly, he lets his imagination soar in the skies of the Divine Form. He says (Verse 5) that his being a dull poet is an advantage as he can linger on each limb for a longer time. He again says (verse 17) that eyes get so much absorbed in what is being seen that what has been seen and what needs to be seen are of no consequence. He feels enchanted by the lustre of the Divine Form. He dwells on the dark complexion of the Lord. Then he looks at the feet of the Lord and savours the look of the enchanting feet over several verses. While he acts as a guide to his readers, his eyes slowly move up the form of the Lord and finally rest in the LordтАЩs face.

An ardent devotee of the Lord will find this work as an emotionally enriching devotional hymn; a Vedantin will find it as a work providing brilliant flashes of Vedantic thought; and a person with a literary bent of mind a sparkling literary gem.

The text along with the authorтАЩs gloss(105 verses)1 has been published by Sri Vani Vilas Press, Srirangam (1927). Based on this book, I have provided for each verse the prose order in Sanskrit and its English translation. Short notes have also been given where required. The intricacies of alaс╣Еk─Бras or the Vedantic thoughts in the verses are beyond the scope of my translation and the short notes. I shall feel gratified if my translation and notes enable the reader to get a glimpse of the emotional, spiritual and literary grandeur of the hymn.

G S S Murthy

______2020

Bangalore

GS ┼Ыr─лniv─Бsam┼лrti

Verses 1-5 are verses of benediction, objection and explanation for composing the hymn:

рдзрдиреНрдпреИрдГ рдпреЛрдЧрдХрд▓рдпрд╛ рд╣реГрджрдп-рдЕрдмреНрдЬ-рдХреЛрд╢рдореН рдЙрджреНрдШрд╛рдЯреНрдп рдЪрд┐рд░рд╛рддреН рдпрдерд╛рд░реБрдЪрд┐ рдЧреГрд╣реНрдпрдорд╛рдгрдГ рдЕрдкрд┐ рдпрдГ рдЕрд╡рд┐рд░рддрдВ рдкрд░рд┐рдкреВрд░реНрдгрд░реВрдкрдГ рдкреНрд░рд╕реНрдлреБрд░рддрд┐ рд╕рдГ рдореБрдХреБрдиреНрджрдГ рд╢рд╛рд╢реНрд╡рддрд┐рдХрдВ рд╢реНрд░реЗрдпрдГрдореЗ рджрд┐рд╢рддреБ ред

GS ┼Ыr─лniv─Бsam┼лrti

May Mukunda endow me with permanent bliss. Although the blessed savour him as per their taste by opening the bud of lotus-like heart through the art of Yoga, He shines in full splendour uninterruptedly.

GS ┼Ыr─лniv─Бsam┼лrti - Note
  1. The Almighty is said to reside thumb-sized in the heart of a person. Those who have mastered the techniques of Yoga are able to access Him and savour Him. Although Yogins have been savouring Him according to their own tastes all the time, He remains undiminished all the time. 2. Mukunda also refers to one of the treasures of Kubera. Use of words тАШko┼ЫaтАЩ (which also means a treasury) and тАШdhanyaтАЩ (which can be interpreted to mean a wealthy person) suggests that Mukunda is an inexhaustible treasure although regularly accessed by wealthy persons namely Yogins. 3. The obvious simile is to savouring of the nectar of lotus flower by prying it open.

GS ┼Ыr─лniv─Бsam┼лrti

Lord! Ultimate Being! No one who is born or who will be born knows the ultimate limit of your Glory. In praising you who is so exalted, will a person like me not be laughed at by the wise?

GS ┼Ыr─лniv─Бsam┼лrti

Lord! The Goddess of speech (Sarasvat─л) praises you by entering even the tongues of great poets wishing to manifest herself by putting upon someone else the blame of having committed unavoidable errors.

GS ┼Ыr─лniv─Бsam┼лrti - Note

The poet obliquely conveys that even the best of poets commit errors while praising you. Even Sarasvat─л, wishing to praise you, tries to put the blame of committing unavoidable errors on great poets by entering their tongues!

GS ┼Ыr─лniv─Бsam┼лrti

O Leader! Vaikuс╣Зс╣нha! Even then, I am describing your form, which adorns the elephant-hill (Hastigiri)2 like a gem and which can be worshipped only by people who have no pride. I am struck by this desire so that by thinking of your name, form and qualities I may benefit.

The hill in K─Бnc─л often called Hasti┼Ыaila.

GS ┼Ыr─лniv─Бsam┼лrti - Note

the poet uses the word тАШmad─БvalaтАЩ to denote an elephant. The word is not listed in standard dictionaries, lexicons.

рд╡рд┐рд╢реНрд╡рд╛рд╕-рдкреНрд░рд╕реНрддреБрддрд┐рдГ

GS ┼Ыr─лniv─Бsam┼лrti - Note

Kumbhaka is a technical word in Yoga associated with breath control (Pr─Бс╣З─Бy─Бma). Pr─Бс╣З─Бy─Бma (controlled breathing) consists of three parts, p┼лraka ( inhaling), kumbhaka ( retaining the inhaled breath) and recaka (exhaling). The poet plays a pun on the word kumbhaka, as kumbha suggests a pitcher which can be used to cross a river.

I consider that your lustre which is as graceful as that of sapphire and which fills the cavity of the three worlds is an ocean which has expanded on account of the pralaya ( swooning, dissolution of the world) experienced by the maidens who are smitten by your beauty.

GS ┼Ыr─лniv─Бsam┼лrti - Note

The poet plays on the word тАЬpralayaтАЭ, which means тАЬswooningтАЭ applicable to the smitten maidens and also means тАЬdissolution of the worldтАЭ which is applicable to the expanding ocean of lustre.

You are white in colour like the moon as per the Vedas and also factually, being the solidified quality of sattva, bereft of rajas and tamas. GS ┼Ыr─лniv─Бsam┼лrti - Note

In that work there is a section тАЬaruс╣З─Бdhikaraс╣Зa тАЭ whch refers to the limited effect of redness in a ritual. The poet says that Jaimini is contradicted by the fact that the red rays emanating from the deityтАЩs feet light up everything.

The stream of rays from your feet which is uniquely flourishing unconquered removes the internal darkness of those who lead a life of restraint. It opens up the lotus-like hearts and acts as a pair of boats for the best of your devotees for crossing the ocean of birth and death.

O Vanquisher of Mura! When the sun steals like a thief the lustre of your feet in the morning, he does not suffer the punishment of hands (decay of rays) being cut off. That is because of his childhood friendship (being the early morning Sun).

GS ┼Ыr─лniv─Бsam┼лrti - Note

The poet plays on the double-meaning words тАЬkaraтАЭ (hand, rays of sun) and тАЬmitraтАЭ(friend, sun) and weaves a metaphor.

GS ┼Ыr─лniv─Бsam┼лrti

If the sun provides lustre to the lotuses which are inseparable associates of your feet, it is as a bribe given by the sun who right from his childhood is engaged in stealing the gems in the form of your feetтАЩs lustre.

GS ┼Ыr─лniv─Бsam┼лrti - Note

The poet refers to the practice of thieves bribing the persons associated with the treasury while stealing a treasure. The Sun has stolen the lustre from the feet of the Lord and the sun has given to the lotuses their lustre as a bribe!

GS ┼Ыr─лniv─Бsam┼лrti

The sun heats up his rays in the fire during the night daily in order that they may gain the lustre of your feetтАЩs rays and when they are taken out of the fire, they become hot after losing the redness quickly. He is, after all, the father of a dull-headed.

GS ┼Ыr─лniv─Бsam┼лrti - Note

In the morning when the sun looks red there is not much heat but later it gets hot. The poet exaggerates by saying that the sun puts his rays in the nights in the fire and takes it out in the morning only to find that it retains the redness sought for only for a short time after which it gets hot. To the possible question why the sun should do the same thing daily, the poet says that he is after all the father of the planet Saturn, whose movements are slow and who is thus considered a dullard. Father of a dullard must be a greater dullard!

Lord! I guess that your foot is a lotus only, being indulged in by the hands of Lakс╣гm─л (nurtured by a lake abounding in auspiciousness) with ascetics who are reciting the sonorous subservient Vedas (with swans cackling in a manner pleasant to hear) and with the ends of foreheads of joyful divine beings bent (looking graceful with bees swarming around blown by the fragrance- carrying wind.)

GS ┼Ыr─лniv─Бsam┼лrti - Note

The poet brings out equivalence between the lotus and LordтАЩs foot by a clever use of double-meaning words.

GS ┼Ыr─лniv─Бsam┼лrti

How is it possible that the lotus which is right from its birth living in slush (sin) is comparable to your feet by the touch of which Ahalya and the Earth were cleansed of their sins?

GS ┼Ыr─лniv─Бsam┼лrti - Note

The poet cleverly uses the word тАЬpaс╣ЕkaтАЭ which can mean slush and sin.

O crest jewel of the elephant hill! I suspect that the lotus realising that it committed a crime against you by assuming equivalence with your feet out of delusion is serving your feet in repentance in the garb of its outline under your feet.

GS ┼Ыr─лniv─Бsam┼лrti - Note

The poet says that the figure of a lotus under the foot of the Lord is indeed lotus itself serving the Lord as a mark of repentance for having assumed equivalence with the feet of the Lord.

GS ┼Ыr─лniv─Бsam┼лrti

O Achyuta! We believe that this mark of lotus on your feet which has stolen the courage of the sprouts from the garden of Indra is the lotus forming a pleasure house of the Lakс╣гm─л of redness resting there as it were.

GS ┼Ыr─лniv─Бsam┼лrti - Note
  1. тАЬLekhaтАЭ means divine beings (AditiтАЩs sons) ; тАЬlekh─Бdhin─БthaтАЭ is their chief, Indra. 2. The sprouts of Nandana garden of Indra are red in colour which they display courageously and the feet of the Lord which are red in colour have stolen their courage. 3. The poet exaggerates to say that Lakс╣гm─л of redness resides in the feet in the form of the outline of a red lotus.

рдорд╣рд╛рдкреБрд░реБрд╖ ! рдпрд╕реНрдпрд╛рдГ рдореВрд▓реЗ рдкрд╛рдж-рдЕрдореНрдмреБрдЬ-рджреНрд╡рдп-рдорд┐рд╖рд╛рддреН рд╕реНрд╡-рдореВрд░реНрддрд┐-рдЕрдиреБрдЧреБрдг-рдЖрдХреГрддрд┐-рд╢рдХреНрддрд┐-рдпреБрдХреНрддрдГ рдХрдорда-рдЕрдзрд┐рд░рд╛рдЬрдГ рд╡рд╕рддрд┐, рд╕рд╛ рддреЗ рдореВрд░реНрддрд┐рдГ рдЕрдЦрд┐рд▓-рд▓реЛрдХ-рд░реВрдкрд╛ (рдЗрддрд┐) рдирд┐рдЧрджреНрдпрддреЗ (рддрддреН) рдЙрдЪрд┐рддрдореН рдПрд╡ ред

GS ┼Ыr─лniv─Бsam┼лrti

O Great Person! The Great Tortoise which has the capacity to assume a form similar to yours lives at the bottom of your form in the garb of your lotus-like feet. It is indeed appropriate that your form is said to be a manifestation of the entire universe.

GS ┼Ыr─лniv─Бsam┼лrti

Lord! The moon, having become jealous of the sun who has twelve forms and desirous of surpassing him and having realized that his own ten forms sparkle in the ten toes of your feet was born to the mind, the eyes (of Atri ) and the ocean (of milk.) (making in all 13 forms!)

GS ┼Ыr─лniv─Бsam┼лrti - Note

What the poet means is that the moon with ten replicas of himself in the form of the toe-nails of the deity took three more births as the son of GodтАЩs mind, of AtriтАЩs eyes and of the ocean. There is a Vedic reference to moon being born of GodтАЩs mind. As per mythology, Atri is the father of the moon and the moon is also said to have been born from the milk-ocean.

The poet has used technical words тАЬ─БropaтАЭ and тАЬadhyavas─БyaтАЭ employed in poetics. ─Аropa is to equate the object of comparison and the subject of comparison clearly expressing their difference, while тАЬadhyavas─Бya тАЭ is equating without expressing the difference. While describing a king, to say, тАЬHe is Brahm─Б without four faces and Hari with only two handsтАЭ is ─Бropa ; to say, тАЬHe is Hari himself who has descended to the earth to protect the worldтАЭ is тАЬadhyavas─БyaтАЭ. The poet says that LordтАЩs navel is in fact a lake as it is the source for the lotus.

GS ┼Ыr─лniv─Бsam┼лrti - Note

The reference is to a Puranic story as per which ┼Ъukra the preceptor of Asuras revived Kaca his disciple who had been burnt by _Sura_s and whose ashes were mixed with a potion offered to ┼Ъukra. ┼Ъukra managed to revive Kaca.

Lotus of the navel is white in colour signifying sattva, the Kaustubha gem is red in colour signifying rajas and the dark hue of the Lord signifies tamas.

GS ┼Ыr─лniv─Бsam┼лrti

I guess the sandal paste (the sandal tree) which is at the centre of your chest in the form of the flower-garden, Nandana, has its branches in the form of your shoulders which have its tender ends in your lotus- like hands.

GS ┼Ыr─лniv─Бsam┼лrti

O Giver of boons! You are taking care of this ruby which comes under the category of Kuruvinda by wearing it as a bangle and, I believe, for that reason, being blind with pride, the ruby tries to show disrespect to the Sun himself.(It outshines the sun by its brilliance) [ By virtue of words with double meaning, the verse also refers to a person who is morally corrupt- pallavar─Бga - but is being taken care of by the king in his army- kaс╣нaka - and because of that reason he disrespects his own father- savit─Б.]

GS ┼Ыr─лniv─Бsam┼лrti - Note

Standard dictionaries do not list тАЬfatherтАЭ as one of the meanings under тАЬsavitс╣ЫтАЭ.

GS ┼Ыr─лniv─Бsam┼лrti

Appayyad─лkс╣гita explains in his commentary that Ruby comes in 4 varieties, namely Padmar─Бga, Kuruvinda, Saugandhika and N─лlagandhi. Pallavar─Бga refers to Kuruvinda variety.

GS ┼Ыr─лniv─Бsam┼лrti

After having seen below your lotus-stalk-like shoulders which have the lustre of sapphire at the lower end, a disc on one side and swan-like conch on the other side, how can we fail to perceive your two hands raised which look like two blossomed lotuses in the river of your lustre?

GS ┼Ыr─лniv─Бsam┼лrti - Note

The poet imagines that in the river of lustre of GodтАЩs form, shoulders are lotus-stalks, hands are blossomed lotuses, and the disc is a Cakrav─Бka bird and the conch a swan.

GS ┼Ыr─лniv─Бsam┼лrti

I believe that you are the person with the cosmic form (extolled in puruс╣гas┼лkta) having as its two sides the conch and the disc more beautiful than the sun and the moon which represent the day and night,

and your string of pearls looking enchanting like stars.

The Great Disc in your right hand, which is as difficult to be looked at as the sun expanding at the time of the Great Dissolution (pralaya) appears to me to be the solidified brilliant valour emanating from your arm which is like a mountain that churns the ocean of Daityas.

Lord! your neck encircled by large blue lotuses sewn along the thread carrying pearls seems like having been encircled by nascent clouds. It looks as if these nascent clouds, after believing that the voice emanating from the throat is from Pralaya clouds, have come near them.

Your face has given rise to Brahm─Б (Brahmins); It is dear to Lakс╣гm─л; It competes with the moon and it is endowed with ears (pericarp of a lotus). Lord! You are a treasure of exceptional qualities. Because of the qualities of your face, who will not realise that it is a beautiful lotus?

Heaps of chaff of your smile wander on the earth in the form of these rays of the moon. (MoonтАЩs rays are the chaff of LordтАЩs smile. LordтАЩs de-chaffed smile is the best medicine for t─Бpatraya.)

GS ┼Ыr─лniv─Бsam┼лrti - Note

The word тАЬt─БpatrayaтАЭ refers to three types of affliction, ─Бdhy─Бtmika, ─Бdhibhautika & ─Бdhidaivika a person suffers during his life. ─Аdhy─Бtmika is associated with bodily and mental causes. ─Аdhibhautika is associated with interactions with other beings. ─Аdhidaivika is associated with seasonal causes, natural calamities etc.

GS ┼Ыr─лniv─Бsam┼лrti

Lord! Where are your eyes, where is the lotus! Even then, the Vedas say that your eyes are like lotus. In the absence of something equal or greater than you, Vedas after all, declare your omnipresence to be like the sky.

GS ┼Ыr─лniv─Бsam┼лrti

O one who is unfriendly to d─Бnava_s_! Your left eye snatches the lustre of the lotus which is proud and discourteous. If the right eye bestows a higher status to the lotus, it is because it is favourably disposed towards it due to politeness.

GS ┼Ыr─лniv─Бsam┼лrti - Note

The left eye of the Lord is the moon. When the moon rises the lotus closes. The right eye of the Lord is the Sun. When the sun rises the lotus blooms. The words used suggest that the manner of the left eye snatching the lustre of the lotus is similar to that of a king snatching the riches of a proud and discourteous nobleman. The poet plays on the word тАЬd─Бkс╣гiс╣ЗyamтАЭ which means тАЬrightsidednessтАЭ and also тАЬfavourably disposed due to politenessтАЭ.

GS ┼Ыr─лniv─Бsam┼лrti

Lord of Hasti┼Ыaila! I do not see any difference between you and your eye. Your eye has the redness of a lotus, is red, black and white by nature, has the appearance of a fish and shines right up to the ear. You are dear to Lakс╣гm─л, you are described as red, black and white (in the Vedas), you took the form of a fish and you are seen as the ultimate goal of the Vedas.

GS ┼Ыr─лniv─Бsam┼лrti - Note

The poet cleverly uses words with double meanings to bring out the apparent similarity between the Lord and his eye.

GS ┼Ыr─лniv─Бsam┼лrti

The group of sweat drops on your temple seems to be in the garb of the group of gems at the bottom of your crown. It looks as if you generated the sweat drops with an intention to create another Brahm─Б as Brahm─Б attained salvation by looking at you.

GS ┼Ыr─лniv─Бsam┼лrti - Note

The verse alludes to a story in Mahopaniс╣гad, wherein it is said that Brahm─Б was born out of the sweat drops of Viс╣гс╣Зu when he was meditating. It is also said that Brahm─Б worshipped Viс╣гс╣Зu through a horse sacrifice and Viс╣гс╣Зu appeared at the end of the sacrifice when Brahm─Б got salvation.

GS ┼Ыr─лniv─Бsam┼лrti

Lotus-eyed Lord! The choicest of sapphire gems on your crown which is made up of a cluster of precious gems do not shine. [The poet exaggerates to say, тАЬWhat shine around your lock of hairs are not the sapphire gems but bees.]

O Lotus-eyed Lord who resides in oneтАЩs mind! May your entire form from head to foot, residing at Hasti┼Ыaila, which is accessible to ladies and realized souls and which manifests as a bundle of ultimate joy shine in my mind all the time.
